  278. I ended up with two sets of these (crazy promos from the e.l.f. website). They're not my favorite brushes, but they're a good way to build up your collection if you're starting from nothing. (I find the e.l.f. brushes that are sold individually and are a bit more expensive -- the ones with black handles -- to be higher quality.)<br /><br />I have not used all of these yet. Thankfully, the intended purpose of each one is printed on the handle, because I'd never be able to guess for some of them. The eyeshadow brushes are fairly high quality; I have yet to find any bristles/hairs falling out of those. I find that the different colors of bristles relate somewhat to the texture. The darker brown bristles are a bit rougher than the golden-colored ones (but none are uncomfortable to use on my face).<br /><br />I'm less satisfied with the larger brushes (for example, the angled one that is second from left in the picture). They are not very thick/full, like some of the bristles came out before I even received them. They've also shed a little bit (although not so much I can't use them).<br /><br />They're pretty easy to clean; I use the e.l.f. brush cleaners (there's a daily spray as well as a weekly shampoo) and hang upside down to dry (so as to prevent water from dripping onto the metal parts). I'd recommend drying hanging upside down (I have a brush hanger for this purpose) because it should prevent rust formation, which should in turn lead to a longer lifetime for these brushes.<br /><br />All-in-all, if you're looking for inexpensive brushes, these are not a bad option. I can definitely see the day I move up to more expensive brushes, purchased individually.   723. When I got these in the mail, they seemed pretty decent for the price. However I washed mine. When I wash mine I stick them in cold water and dawn to loosen the powder. Make sure the water is clear, then give them a final rinse in a little vinegar. My other brushes with the plastic handles handled the washing just fine. These just fell apart, I didn't leave them to soak for that long knowing that some of the brushes may not hold up. The hairs are comming out, the paint is cracking on the handle, and they are detaching from the handle. Don't buy these its a waste of your hard earned money. Sonia Kashuk hold up better, I buy them on sale. I also go to craft stores and buy brushes with real hair. They last for ever and you can give them a good cleaning without worrying about them falling apart.
